title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_essa_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip_essa-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><br />Passenger Traffic, ACI Europe<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Stockholm Arlanda Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>ARN</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>ESSA</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/Sigtuna_Municipality" title="Sigtuna Municipality">Sigtuna Municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, near the town of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4rsta" title="M\xc3\xa4rsta">M\xc3\xa4rsta</a>, 37 kilometres (23&#160;mi) north<sup id="cite_ref-aip_essa_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip_essa-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a> and nearly 40 kilometres (25&#160;mi) south-east of <a href="/wiki/Uppsala" title="Uppsala">Uppsala</a>. The airport is located within <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_County" title="Stockholm County">Stockholm County</a> and the province of <a href="/wiki/Uppland" title="Uppland">Uppland</a>. It is the largest airport in Sweden and the third-largest airport in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_airports_in_the_Nordic_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="List of the largest airports in the Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a>. The airport is the major gateway to international air travel for large parts of Sweden. Arlanda Airport was used by close to 27 million passengers in 2017, with 21.2 million international passengers and 5.5 million domestic.<sup id="cite_ref-statistics_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Stockholm Arlanda Airport is the larger of Stockholm\'s two airports. The other, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Bromma_Airport" title="Stockholm Bromma Airport">Stockholm\xe2\x80\x93Bromma</a>, is located north-west of the city\'s centre but can be used only by a small number of smaller aircraft. The smaller airports <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Skavsta_Airport" title="Stockholm Skavsta Airport">Stockholm-Skavsta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_V%C3%A4ster%C3%A5s_Airport" title="Stockholm V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s Airport">Stockholm-V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s</a> are both located around 100 kilometres (60&#160;mi) away from the Swedish capital. Stockholm Arlanda serves as a major hub for <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Facilities"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Facilities</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Runways"><span class="toctext">Terminals</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-5"><a href="#Terminal_2_\xe2\x80\x93_International_(Arlanda_South)"><span class="tocnumber">2.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Terminal 2 \xe2\x80\x93 International (Arlanda South)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-6"><a href="#Terminal_3_\xe2\x80\x93_Regional_domestic_(Arlanda_South)"><span (Arlanda North)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Cargo_facilities"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cargo destinations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Passenger"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Passenger</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Cargo"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Cargo</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Statistics"><span <span class="toctext">Winter time operations and snow clearing</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Aircraft_hangars_and_maintenance_facilities"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Aircraft hangars and maintenance facilities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#VIP_flights_and_services"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">VIP flights and services</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Ground_transportation"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Ground transportation</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Rail"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Rail</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Bus"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bus</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Road"><span class="toctext">Taxi</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Uppsala_and_farther_north"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">Uppsala and farther north</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Environment"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Environment</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Incidents_and_accidents"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Incidents and accidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_%281%29.jpg/170px-Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_%281%29.jpg/255px-Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_%281%29.jpg/340px-Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2672" data-file-height="3543" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inaugural_of_Arlanda_Airport_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gustaf_VI_Adolf_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Gustaf VI Adolf of Sweden">King Gustaf VI Adolf</a> presiding over the ceremony which officially inaugurated Stockholm\xe2\x80\x93Arlanda Airport (1 April 1962)</div></div></div>\n<p>The airport was first used in 1959 but only for practice flights. It opened for limited civil traffic in 1960, and in 1962 the official opening ceremony took place. It was used from the start for intercontinental traffic because the runway at Bromma was too short. Scandinavian Airlines started using <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-8" title="Douglas DC-8">Douglas DC-8s</a> on North American routes. The airport was also used very early by <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a>. The name <i>Arlanda</i> was decided after a competition prior to the airport opening. It is derived from Arland, an old name for the parish <a href="/wiki/%C3%84rlinghundra" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x84rlinghundra">\xc3\x84rlinghundra</a> (now Husby-\xc3\x84rlinghundra in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4rsta" title="M\xc3\xa4rsta">M\xc3\xa4rsta</a>) where the airport is situated. The \'-a\' was added in analogy with other Swedish place names ending with -landa and also plays on the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> verb "landa", which means "to land". The 1960s and 1970s saw increases in traffic with scheduled traffic and charter traffic. The <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> jumbojet started to be used in the 1970s, both on one-stop scheduled flights to New York and on weekend nonstop charters to the Canary Islands. Domestic flights to Gothenburg, Malm\xc3\xb6, Lule\xc3\xa5 and Kiruna were operated by SAS <a href="/wiki/DC-9" class="mw-redirect" title="DC-9">DC-9s</a> from Arlanda since they were considered too noisy to be used at downtown Bromma. The rest of domestic traffic operated out of Bromma and all international traffic out of Arlanda.\n</p><p>In 1983 the domestic traffic operated by <a href="/wiki/Linjeflyg" title="Linjeflyg">Linjeflyg</a> moved from Bromma to Arlanda, using the terminal now known as Terminal 4. In 1990 two new domestic terminals called "Domestic 2 and 3" were built south of the first domestic terminal. In 1992 the terminal 2 was partly abandoned because of traffic decrease. It started to be used for international traffic the year after, and the main domestic and international terminals were renumbered into 4 and 5. The third runway was built between 1998 and 2002. However, a recession in 2002 delayed its opening until 2003. At that time protests were raised by people living under its <a href="/wiki/Flight_path" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight path">flight path</a> in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Upplands_V%C3%A4sby" title="Upplands V\xc3\xa4sby">Upplands V\xc3\xa4sby</a>. Traffic has recovered since and is now showing healthy increases but the third runway is only used during peak hours for environmental reasons. In September 2010 the first <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> superjumbo landed at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early 2014, <a href="/wiki/Swedavia" title="Swedavia">Swedavia</a> announced plans for further expansions of the airport terminal complex, including the construction of an additional pier for Terminal 5 in order to better accommodate larger aircraft such as the Airbus A380 and Boeing 747-8 and address forecasts of rising passenger numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The plans were approved by the Environmental Court of Appeals in December 2014, and construction was scheduled to commence in the spring of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the spring of 2020, most flights were cancelled due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pressreleases-april-2020_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pressreleases-april-2020-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SAS_Group" title="SAS Group">SAS</a> decided to from 6 April 2020 fly only four domestic departures and four domestic arrivals from Arlanda, plus some international<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> while Norwegian cancelled all flights from Arlanda except to Oslo.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Terminal 2, 3 and 4 closed and terminal 5 handled all passengers during this period (started March, ongoing November)<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Flygplatsstatistik_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flygplatsstatistik-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The passenger figures were 97.7% lower in April 2020 than in April 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-Flygplatsstatistik_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flygplatsstatistik-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pressreleases-april-2020_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pressreleases-april-2020-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The figured picked up later, but were still more than 80% less per month than 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Terminal_2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Arlanda_Terminal_2.JPG/220px-Arlanda_Terminal_2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Terminal_2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Check-In_at_Stockholm_Arlanda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Check-In_at_Stockholm_Arlanda.jpg/220px-Check-In_at_Stockholm_Arlanda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Check-In_at_Stockholm_Arlanda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-In at Terminal 2</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg/220px-Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg/330px-Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg/440px-Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2985" data-file-height="1941" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Skycity_shopping.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shopping and restaurant area in Sky City between terminals 4 and 5</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ARNterm5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/ARNterm5.jpg/220px-ARNterm5.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/ARNterm5.jpg/330px-ARNterm5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/ARNterm5.jpg/440px-ARNterm5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3463" data-file-height="2305" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ARNterm5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 5</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg/220px-Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg/330px-Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg/440px-Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stockholm-Arlanda_Airport_Terminal_5_c.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 5 check-in area</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Arlanda has three <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a>: Runway 1 (01L/19R), Runway 2 (08/26) and Runway 3 (01R/19L). Runway 1 is 3,301&#160;m (10,830&#160;ft)<sup id="cite_ref-lfv.se_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lfv.se-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> long and can handle take-offs and landings of the heaviest aircraft in use today. Runways 2 and 3 are 2,500&#160;m (8,202&#160;ft) long.<sup id="cite_ref-lfv.se_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lfv.se-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> As indicated, runways 1 and 3 are parallel runways that can be operated independently of one another. Runways 1 and 3 are equipped with <a href="/wiki/CAT_IIIa" class="mw-redirect" title="CAT IIIa">CAT III</a> systems for instrument landings.<sup id="cite_ref-lfv.se_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lfv.se-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The airport can handle simultaneous take offs and landings using runways 1 and 3 at the same time. Simultaneous aircraft takeoffs and landings can be performed in <a href="/wiki/Instrument_meteorological_conditions" title="Instrument meteorological conditions">instrument meteorological conditions</a> (IMC). Runway 3 (01R/19L) is reached from the main terminal area via <a href="/wiki/Taxiway_bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxiway bridge">taxiway bridges</a> constructed to be able to handle the heaviest and largest airplanes in traffic. Since runway 3 (01R/19L) is located at a distance from the terminals a deicing area is placed close to the runway to avoid too long time between deicing and take off in winter conditions. Another deicing area is located in connection with the southern ramp area close to take off positions at runway 01L. There are high speed taxiway exits from all runways, except runway 08, to enable aircraft to exit the runways quickly after landing. That increases runway capacity during rush hours. Use of parallel taxiways around the terminal area separates arriving and departing traffic. Arlanda can handle all aircraft types in service including the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport has four terminals. Terminals 2 and 5 are used for international flights. Domestic flights are in Terminals 3 and 4. The new central building, Arlanda North, opened in late 2003, connecting terminal 5 with the newly built Pier F. All international flights handled by <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">SAS</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> partners use the new central building. An Arlanda South building, connecting terminals 2, 3 and 4 was also planned, but construction is currently suspended for lack of funds. In the terminal areas and the shopping area "Sky City" there are restaurants, shopping facilities, bars etc. to cater to the needs for passengers and visitors to the airport. There are hotels both at the airport in connection with the terminals and in its surroundings. There are also conference facilities at the airport.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_2_.E2.80.93_International_.28Arlanda_South.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2_\xe2\x80\x93_International_(Arlanda_South)">Terminal 2 \xe2\x80\x93 International (Arlanda South)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Terminal 2 \xe2\x80\x93 International (Arlanda South)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<dl><dd><ul><li>Terminal 2 (gates 61\xe2\x80\x9372) was initially built in 1990 for use by SAS as a domestic terminal. The terminal was designed to enable short turnaround times for aircraft, increased efficiency, and short walking distances, then without security checks and with most passengers having only hand luggage, allowed to show up 10 minutes before departure. It had double walk bridges designed for both doors of MD-80. However, SAS decided to leave the terminal because of decreases in passenger traffic on domestic routes. For a while the terminal was used by other airlines like Transwede Airways for both domestic and international services, but the terminal is now used only for international flights. Security checks, a larger luggage claim area, more shops and restaurants have had to be added over the years, making the terminal fairly small. However, in 2013 it was extended with a new floor level, which now has restaurants and a lounge. Terminal 2 has 8 aircraft parking stands with passenger bridges.</li>\n<li>As of 29 May 2012, Norwegian relocated its international flights from Terminal 2 to Terminal 5 ousting Air France and Czech Airlines to Terminal 2.</li>\n<li>In April 2013, British Airways and Finnair relocated to the newly renovated Terminal 2.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></dd></dl>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_3_.E2.80.93_Regional_domestic_.28Arlanda_South.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3_\xe2\x80\x93_Regional_domestic_(Arlanda_South)">Terminal 3 \xe2\x80\x93 Regional domestic (Arlanda South)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Terminal 3 \xe2\x80\x93 Regional domestic (Arlanda South)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<dl><dd><ul><li>Terminal 3 (gates 51\xe2\x80\x9359) was built in 1990 for regional aircraft. There is a caf\xc3\xa9 there. People walk outdoors from the gates and board the planes with airstairs. Access is through terminal 2, with a 200 m walking distance. As with terminal 2, it was built without security checks, which were added after <a href="/wiki/9/11" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11">2001</a>. There has been a decline in passenger numbers for smaller connections in Sweden.</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_4_.E2.80.93_Domestic_.28Arlanda_South.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_4_\xe2\x80\x93_Domestic_(Arlanda_South)">Terminal 4 \xe2\x80\x93 Domestic (Arlanda South)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Terminal 4 \xe2\x80\x93 Domestic (Arlanda South)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<dl><dd><ul><li>Terminal 4, formerly <b>Inrikes 1</b> (gates 30\xe2\x80\x9344) was originally designed for the Swedish domestic carrier <a href="/wiki/Linjeflyg" title="Linjeflyg">Linjeflyg</a>, and initiated in 1983. <a href="/wiki/Linjeflyg" title="Linjeflyg">Linjeflyg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> moved all operations from Stockholm\xe2\x80\x93Bromma Airport to the new terminal at <a href="/wiki/Arlanda" class="mw-redirect" title="Arlanda">Arlanda</a> in 1984. That was made to assemble the domestic and international departures between <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linjeflyg" title="Linjeflyg">Linjeflyg</a>. Because of increasing popularity, the terminal soon got too small. For that reason, Inrikes 2 was set up for <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">SAS</a>, who moved all domestic flights from Inrikes 1 to the new terminal in 1990.</li>\n<li>Because of a recession in Swedish economy <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">SAS</a> moved back in 1992 and again the two carriers shared the terminal. Also in 1992 the terminal got a new name, Terminal 4. Since 1999 the terminal has had its own express station for high-speed trains, connecting the terminal with Stockholm Central Station and Terminal 5. In 2006, the terminal underwent a major renovation, the first since it was built in 1983.</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_5_.E2.80.93_International_.28Arlanda_North.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_5_\xe2\x80\x93_International_(Arlanda_North)">Terminal 5 \xe2\x80\x93 International (Arlanda North)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminal 5 \xe2\x80\x93 International (Arlanda North)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<dl><dd><ul><li>Terminal 5 (gates 1\xe2\x80\x9324 &amp; F26\xe2\x80\x93F69) is the largest of the passenger terminals at the airport and in use for international flights. All intercontinental flights and other international flights, except those in terminal 2, operate from terminal 5. The terminal has three piers equipped with 31 aircraft parking stands with passenger bridges. There are also a number of remote aircraft parking positions serving the terminal. Terminal 5 has restaurants, bars and shopping areas. The first stage of the terminal was inaugurated in 1976. Terminal 5 has since been expanded with a new passenger pier F. By 2040 terminal 5 will be expanded with another pier, pier G, which will help the airport accommodate 40 million passengers compared with the 25 million today. The new pier will be designed to handle bigger aircraft models such as the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the scheduled services listed, all charter flights are handled at Terminal 5. The terminal is (like terminal 4 and Sky City) connected to Stockholm Central station by high-speed trains.</li></ul></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cargo_facilities">Cargo facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cargo facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Stockholm Arlanda has extensive cargo flight activity. There is a cargo area with cargo terminals and cargo transit facilities in the southern part of the airport area. The cargo area is labeled "Cargo City" with warehouses operated by Cargo Center,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> DHL, Swedish postal service (Posten) and Spirit Air Cargo.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> A large part of mail and express parcels from Sweden is handled through the facilities at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> SAS Cargo has its cargo operation east of the passenger terminals close to the SAS hangars.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dedicated scheduled cargo flights are operated by Korean Air with Boeing 747 cargo aircraft, as well as <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>. DHL, FedEx and UPS operate express freight services at the airport. West Air Sweden and Amapola operate shorter cargo sectors. A number of airlines operate ad hoc cargo flights with various equipment. Outsize cargo is frequently hauled with the <a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-124" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonov An-124">Antonov An-124</a> and similar cargo planes. TNT had their operations at Arlanda but have since moved to V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s Airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Swedavia" title="Swedavia">Swedavia</a>, the Swedish airport management company, has its head office in the airport control tower facility.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The company Sollentuna Cabin Interiors has its head office in Hangar 4 at Arlanda.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nOxford Aviation Academy has a flight simulator centre for some of the most common airliners of today (like Boeing 737) at Arlanda. Arlanda has hangars and <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_maintenance" title="Aircraft maintenance">aircraft maintenance</a> facilities operated by SAS Scandinavian Airlines and Priority Aero Maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-priority.aero_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-priority.aero-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TUI_fly_Nordic" title="TUI fly Nordic">TUI fly Nordic</a> based at the airport also has a large hangar for widebody jets. There is also a helicopter repair facility operated by Patria Helicopters.<sup id="cite_ref-swedishaviationgroup.com_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swedishaviationgroup.com-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A decommissioned Boeing 747 jumbo jet renovated into a hostel, the <a href="/wiki/Jumbo_Stay" title="Jumbo Stay">Jumbo Stay</a> (formerly Jumbo Hostel), is located at the entrance to Arlanda Airport. There are four additional hotels at the airport (Clarion Hotel Arlanda Airport, Radisson Blu Arlandia Hotel, Radisson Blu SkyCity Hotel and Rest and Fly); in addition there are several hotels nearby with transfer buses.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a 0.4%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Winter_time_operations_and_snow_clearing">Winter time operations and snow clearing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Winter time operations and snow clearing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg/220px-Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg/330px-Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg/440px-Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="755" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lufthansajetinsnowatarlanda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> Airbus A321 in a special retro livery taxiing in snow at Arlanda</div></div></div>\n<p>Arlanda has a policy to never close due to snowfall.<sup id="cite_ref-snowrem_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snowrem-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>  Arlanda is exposed to <a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">lake-effect snowfalls</a>, where ice cold air from the northeast in combination with open water in the Baltic Sea causes heavy snowfall.  During heavy snowfall at least one runway stays open but in bad weather condition there may be delays even if flight operations continue at all times. Not just runways need to be cleared, aprons and aircraft parking areas need snow clearing as well. It is an advantage that there are three runways allowing two open runways when one is cleared at lighter snowfall. The airport has a total of 250 000 m<sup>2</sup> to clear from snow and ice, at the same time as the aircraft continue taking off and landing.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> During the colder half of the year Stockholm Arlanda has about 65 seasonally hired snow removal staff. Together with permanent staff, they form a team of 100 people who provide snow removal services. Special routes are planned for sweeping teams, which clear each route at intervals of 35 to 45 minutes. The sweeping teams are directed via radio from the air traffic control tower. When snow removal is completed on each runway the surface is tested by a friction vehicle, which measures friction value. The airport announces the friction value, and then it is each pilot who decides whether the value is sufficient for a landing. The friction value determines how often a runway must be ploughed and treated with antiskid agent.<sup id="cite_ref-snowrem_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snowrem-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_hangars_and_maintenance_facilities">Aircraft hangars and maintenance facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Aircraft hangars and maintenance facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG/220px-TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG/330px-TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG/440px-TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="816" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TUIflyNordic767-300ERinArlandahangarl1200.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Boeing 767-300ER in TUI fly Nordic hangar at Arlanda</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/SAS_Technical_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="SAS Technical Services">SAS Technical Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/TUI_fly_Nordic" title="TUI fly Nordic">TUI fly Nordic</a> and Priority Aero Maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-priority.aero_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-priority.aero-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> have large aircraft hangars and maintenance facilities at the airport. SAS Technical Services is headquartered at Arlanda and has hangar facilities suitable for widebody aircraft up to the size of Boeing 747-400s. The first part of the hangar complex was built to handle SAS\' fleet of DC-8s. There are a number of positions on each side of the building initially built to handle the type. The hangar space are nowa used mostly for Boeing 737s and A320s. The Boeing 747 hangar was inaugurated at the time when Scandinavian Airlines received their first Boeing 747s in the beginning of the 70s. It is large enough to handle a Boeing 747 and two 737 sized airplanes at the same time. The offices of <a href="/wiki/SAS_Technical_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="SAS Technical Services">SAS Technical Services</a> are situated in connection with the hangars. In the early days of the airport these hangars provided heavy maintenance for members of the KSSU group,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> which included KLM, SAS, Swissair and UTA. A number of other airlines, such as Thai Airways International, also maintained their aircraft in those hangars. Now the main user is Scandinavian Airlines. TUI fly Nordic has a hangar able to handle their largest aircraft, the Boeing 787-9.  Priority Aero Maintenance has its facilities in the eastern part of the airport. They provide heavy aircraft maintenance for a number of aircraft including MD-80, a common type to be overhauled by the company.\n</p><p>There is also a hangar in the southern part of the airport, built by the former Swedish domestic airline <a href="/wiki/Linjeflyg" title="Linjeflyg">Linjeflyg</a>. It is used mainly by regional aircraft.\n</p><p>Helicopter hangars and maintenance facilities are found at the very eastern part of the airport operated by Patria Helicopters.<sup id="cite_ref-swedishaviationgroup.com_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swedishaviationgroup.com-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="VIP_flights_and_services">VIP flights and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: VIP flights and services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Arlanda, as the main airport serving the Swedish capital, is also used by VIP-flights<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> using <a href="/wiki/Business_jets" class="mw-redirect" title="Business jets">business jets</a>. Government officials and celebrities are frequent visitors. In April 2011, the then-<a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Russian_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman of the Russian Government">Chairman of the Russian Government</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> visited Stockholm with a <a href="/wiki/Russian_presidential_aircraft" title="Russian presidential aircraft">couple of large jet airplanes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Japan" title="Emperor of Japan">Emperor of Japan</a> has also visited Arlanda with his <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In September 2013, <a href="/wiki/U.S._President" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. President">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, made an official visit to Sweden with <i><a href="/wiki/Air_Force_One" title="Air Force One">Air Force One</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> EU-meetings and exhibitions in the Stockholm area also bring special flights to the airport. Various private companies use their business jets to attend meetings in the Stockholm area. Some VIP-flights also go to downtown <a href="/wiki/Bromma_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Bromma Airport">Bromma Airport</a>, but since Bromma has limited operational hours many go to Arlanda instead. European Flight Service has a <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_G500/G550" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulfstream G500/G550">Grumman Gulfstream</a> G550 based at Arlanda for VIP flights.\n</p><p>Arlanda has several VIP lounges.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>  They allow travelers to meet their planes on the tarmac.  The VIP area can also hold weddings, with or without a flight.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  The airport also holds weddings in the control tower.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td class="RMr" colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Karlberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Karlberg">Karlberg</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td class="RMl" class="RMd"></div>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td class="RMr" colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Station" title="Stockholm City Station">Stockholm City</a> <a class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td style="padding:0 0 0 3px;min-width:45px;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="border-top: 5px solid #F9F9F9;border-bottom: 5px solid 6px 6px">\n<table class="nogrid routemap" style="font-size:107.95454545455%">\n\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="RMl" colspan="2">\n</td>\n<td class="RMl1">\n</td>\n<td class="RMir"><div><img alt="" class="RMl1">\n</td>\n<td class="RMir"><div><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/BSicon_STRq.svg/20px-BSicon_STRq.svg.png" decoding="async" title="STRq" width="20" class="RMir"><div><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/BSicon_STRq_orange.svg/20px-BSicon_STRq_orange.svg.png" decoding="async" title="STRq orange" width="20" class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td class="RMr" colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Arlanda_Express" title="Arlanda Express">Arlanda Express</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="padding:0 3px 0 0;">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMl1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td style="padding:0 0 0 3px;width:3.375em;min-width:3.375em;min-width:45px;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The fastest way to the airport from <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Central_Station" title="Stockholm Central Station">Stockholm Central Station</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Arlanda_Express" title="Arlanda Express">Arlanda Express</a> high-speed train service, making the trip in 20 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm,_Sweden_(4617050400).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm%2C_Sweden_%284617050400%29.jpg/220px-Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm%2C_Sweden_%284617050400%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm%2C_Sweden_%284617050400%29.jpg/330px-Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm%2C_Sweden_%284617050400%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm%2C_Sweden_%284617050400%29.jpg/440px-Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm%2C_Sweden_%284617050400%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1607" data-file-height="1206" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Airport_-_Stockholm,_Sweden_(4617050400).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Taxi at Arlanda airport</div></div></div>\n<p>It is possible to use the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_commuter_rail" title="Stockholm commuter rail">Stockholm commuter rail</a> (Pendelt\xc3\xa5g) between Uppsala C and central and southern Stockholm. The route takes 38 minutes between Arlanda C station and Stockholm C.<sup id="cite_ref-sl.se_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sl.se-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The fare is higher from Arlanda compared to other journeys on the commuter rail network because the railway to Arlanda is privately owned, with passengers over 18 having to pay a passage fee of 120SEK to enter or exit the airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Flygbussarna" title="Flygbussarna">Flygbussarna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flixbus" title="Flixbus">Flixbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Storstockholms_Lokaltrafik" title="Storstockholms Lokaltrafik">SL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kollektivtrafikf%C3%B6rvaltningen_UL" title="Kollektivtrafikf\xc3\xb6rvaltningen UL">UL</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vy_bus4you" title="Vy bus4you">Vy bus4you</a> operate services to and from Arlanda. Flygbussarna operates frequent departures to Stockholm, while Flixbus and bus4you operate coach services to different destinations in Sweden. SL is the public transport operator of Stockholm L\xc3\xa4n, whilst UL is the public transport operator in Uppsala L\xc3\xa4n. SL operates a few bus lines to and from Arlanda, the most popular line being route 583 to M\xc3\xa4rsta railway station (from where SL commuter trains to Stockholm depart, for much cheaper than from Arlanda because of the exit fee charge there), which leaves every 10 minutes for the most of the day. ULs most popular line to Arlanda is route 801 to Uppsala, which leaves every 30 minutes between 04:00 and 01:00. There are a few additional departures during peak times. An additional shuttle bus operates between Arlanda and the nearby <a href="/wiki/Jumbo_Stay" title="Jumbo Stay">Jumbo Stay</a> hostel, located just outside the airport grounds.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The motorway <a href="/wiki/European_route_E4" title="European route E4">E4</a> goes past the airport and connects Arlanda with central Stockholm as well as Uppsala and other cities further north.\nTerminal parking, short-term and long-term parking is available at the airport. The low price long-term parking requires a free shuttle bus ride. The bus departs every 8\xe2\x80\x9315 minutes. There are rental car facilities at the airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">Taxi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Taxi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>All taxi companies are required to offer fixed prices from the airport (one can still request use of the taxi meter). Most major companies also offer fixed prices to the airport.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG/220px-Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG/330px-Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG/440px-Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arlanda_Express_X3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arlanda Express</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Uppsala_and_farther_north">Uppsala and farther north</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Uppsala and farther north">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There is a <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_commuter_rail" title="Stockholm commuter rail">Stockholm commuter rail</a> service (Pendelt\xc3\xa5g) between <a href="/wiki/Uppsala" title="Uppsala">Uppsala</a> and Stockholm, but on <a href="/wiki/Upplands_Lokaltrafik" class="mw-redirect" title="Upplands Lokaltrafik">Uppsala county tickets</a> north of Arlanda, which takes 18 minutes from Arlanda Central to its <a href="/wiki/Uppsala_Central_Station" title="Uppsala Central Station">Uppsala C</a> terminus.<sup id="cite_ref-sl.se_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sl.se-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Buses operated by <i>Upplands Lokaltrafik</i> travel between Stockholm Arlanda Airport and <a href="/wiki/Uppsala" title="Uppsala">Uppsala</a> (bus no. 801) as well as <a href="/wiki/Enk%C3%B6ping" title="Enk\xc3\xb6ping">Enk\xc3\xb6ping</a> to the southwest (bus no. 579/803) and <a href="/wiki/Almunge" title="Almunge">Almunge</a> (bus no. 806) to the northeast.\n</p><p>Long-distance trains called <a href="/wiki/Inter-city_rail" title="Inter-city rail">Intercity</a>, Regionalt\xc3\xa5g (Regional train) or <a href="/wiki/X_2000" title="X 2000">X2000</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/SJ_AB" title="SJ AB">SJ</a> go to locations north of Stockholm Arlanda Airport and south of Stockholm. Passengers are not permitted to use long-distance trains to go to <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Central_Station" title="Stockholm Central Station">Stockholm Central Station</a>; no such tickets are sold.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>There is an ongoing work to limit Arlanda\'s negative impact on the environment. In an effort to save electricity, buildings at Arlanda use <a href="/wiki/District_heating" title="District heating">district heating</a> with biofuels and <a href="/wiki/District_cooling" title="District cooling">district cooling</a> with water from a nearby lake. The take off charges for aircraft are partly based on the environmental performance of the aircraft and Arlanda is experimenting with Continuous Descent Approaches and landings, often referred to as "green landings".<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jet_fuel" title="Jet fuel">Jet fuel</a> is since around 2006 delivered by boat to <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A4vle" title="G\xc3\xa4vle">G\xc3\xa4vle</a> and via train to Brista close to <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4rsta" title="M\xc3\xa4rsta">M\xc3\xa4rsta</a> and from there through pipeline. Previously fuel was delivered by ship to V\xc3\xa4rtahamnen in Stockholm and then by trucks through Stockholm city to Arlanda. The airport also takes measures to promote the use of <a href="/wiki/Bio_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bio fuel">bio fuel</a> in taxis operating to and from the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the most interesting eco-friendly systems Stockholm Arlanda Airport uses is their unique heating and cooling system for their hangar, terminals, and other buildings on the airfield. There innovative system uses a series of wells, linked to a large underground aquifer. The water from the underground source is plumbed up and into the facilities air system, which controls the temperature of the air coming from the vents. In the summertime, the underground water remains cooler than the surface. That allows the terminals to be cooled off without using extra energy that an air conditioner would require. Then, in the winter months, the underground water remains warmer than the surface. The water is then plumbed to a control/heating unit, which uses biofuel to heat the water to a temperature appropriate for warming up the buildings.\n</p><p>The heated water is also used to heat pads of cement on the ramp and near the large hangar doors. Ut is a very efficient way to keep the doors and ramps clear of ice. After the water is run through the system, it is then all replaced back into the aquifer to be used again. The unique aquifer system is one of Arlanda\'s most defining environmentally friendly designs.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>1 November 1969: A <a href="/wiki/Linjeflyg" title="Linjeflyg">Linjeflyg</a> <a href="/wiki/Convair_240" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair 240">Convair 440</a> registered as <i>SE-BSU</i> suffered an accident while being used for training purposes. After a simulated engine failure at <a href="/wiki/Takeoff" title="Takeoff">takeoff</a> the left wing contacted the ground and the aircraft crash-landed after the nose and main landing gear collapsed. None of the four persons on board were killed, but the aircraft was written off.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>5 January 1970: A <a href="/wiki/Spantax" title="Spantax">Spantax</a> <a href="/wiki/Convair_990" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair 990">Convair 990</a> registered as <i>EC-BNM</i> on a ferry flight from Stockholm Arlanda Airport to <a href="/wiki/Zurich_Airport" title="Zurich Airport">Zurich Airport</a> (ZRH) <a href="/wiki/1970_Spantax_Convair_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="1970 Spantax Convair crash">crashed</a> while climbing after take-off. The aircraft had been scheduled for a charter flight earlier in the day, but the flight was cancelled after the no. 4 engine developed trouble. The decision was made to ferry the aircraft using three engines to Zurich for repairs and the aircraft departed at 10:54&#160;p.m. from runway 19 (currently runway 19R). The aircraft contacted trees approximately 1,800&#160;m (5,906&#160;ft) from the point of lift-off. Five of the 10 passengers and crew on board were killed and the aircraft was written off.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>14 July 1973: A <a href="/wiki/Sterling_Airlines" title="Sterling Airlines">Sterling Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Sud_Aviation_Caravelle" title="Sud Aviation Caravelle">Sud Aviation Caravelle</a> registered as <i>OY-SAN</i> taxied into an obstruction and was written off as being damaged beyond repair.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>25 January 1974: <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Sud_Aviation_Caravelle" title="Sud Aviation Caravelle">Sud Aviation Caravelle</a> registered as <i>OY-KRA</i> was damaged beyond repair and written off.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>26 May 1977: An <a href="/wiki/Antonov_24" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonov 24">Antonov 24</a> belonging to <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a> registered as <i>SSSR-46806</i> on a scheduled flight from <a href="/wiki/Donetsk_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Donetsk Airport">Donetsk Airport</a> (DOK) to <a href="/wiki/Riga_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Riga Airport">Riga Airport</a> (RIX) was hijacked by a single hijacker who demanded to be taken to Sweden where the hijacker surrendered releasing the 23 passengers and crew.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>27 February 1979: An <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a> <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_154" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupolev 154">Tupolev 154</a> on a flight from Oslo to Stockholm with a continuation to Moscow was taken over by three hijackers. After landing in Stockholm they were overpowered by the aircraft\'s crew.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>6 January 1987: A <a href="/wiki/Transwede" class="mw-redirect" title="Transwede">Transwede</a> <a href="/wiki/Sud_Aviation_Caravelle" title="Sud Aviation Caravelle">Sud Aviation Caravelle</a> registered as <i>SE-DEC</i> on a non-scheduled flight from Stockholm\xe2\x80\x93Arlanda Airport to <a href="/wiki/Alicante_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Alicante Airport">Alicante Airport</a> (ALC) encountered problems after take-off most likely caused by ice. The aircraft hit the runway hard causing the landing gear to fail and the aircraft slid off the runway and caught fire. None of the 27 passengers and crew was killed but the aircraft was written off and subsequently used by the airport\'s <a href="/wiki/ARFF" class="mw-redirect" title="ARFF">ARFF</a> as a fire and rescue training aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>27 December 1991: <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines_Flight_751" title="Scandinavian Airlines Flight 751">Scandinavian Airlines Flight 751</a>, a <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-81" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-81">McDonnell Douglas MD-81</a>, registered as <i>OY-KHO</i>, a scheduled flight from Stockholm\xe2\x80\x93Arlanda Airport to <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Frederic_Chopin_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Frederic Chopin Airport">Warsaw-Frederic Chopin Airport</a> (WAW) with a stopover at <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen-Kastrup Airport</a> (CPH) crashed shortly after take-off because of a dual engine failure when clear ice, which had formed during the night, was not properly removed during de-icing, broke off and was ingested into the engines. None of the 129 passengers and crew was killed but the aircraft was written off.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>20 February 1993: A hijacker on board an <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a> <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_134" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupolev 134">Tupolev 134</a> on a scheduled flight between <a href="/wiki/Tyumen" title="Tyumen">Tyumen</a> Airport (TJM) and <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">Saint Petersburg-Pulkovo Airport</a> (LED) demanded to be taken to the United States. The aircraft first made a refueling stop in <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">Tallinn</a> where 30 passengers were released, and the aircraft was flown to Stockholm, where the hijacker demanded a larger aircraft to be flown to the U.S. After having released 12 more passengers, the hijacker, who was accompanied by his wife and child, surrendered, releasing the remaining 40 passengers and crew.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>7 October 1997: A <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a> belonging to <a href="/wiki/Tarom" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarom">Tarom</a> registered as <i>YR-BCM</i> on a scheduled flight from <a href="/wiki/Henri_Coand%C4%83_International_Airport" title="Henri Coand\xc4\x83 International Airport">Bucharest-Otopeni International Airport</a> (OTP) to Stockholm\xe2\x80\x93Arlanda Airport suffered a failure of the nosewheel steering after touching down heavily on runway 26. As the airplane slowed down the commander discovered that he could not control the aircraft, which left the runway and continued into the grassy area to on the right side. The aircraft slowed down softly and when it came to a stop the passengers and crew were able to disembark using the normal exits. The aircraft was written off and taken to <a href="/wiki/Halmstad" title="Halmstad">Halmstad</a> by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Le_Caravelle_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Le Caravelle Club (page does not exist)">Le Caravelle Club</a> to be used as a fire trainer.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>8 October 1999: A <a href="/wiki/Saab_2000" title="Saab 2000">Saab 2000</a> belonging to <a href="/wiki/SAS_Commuter" title="SAS Commuter">SAS Commuter</a> registered as <i>SE-SLF</i> called "Eir Viking" ran into a closed hangar door. At the time it was supposedly being taxied by two engineers or technicians.  The two people on board received some injuries and the aircraft was written off.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a V\xc3\xa4ster\xc3\xa5s Airport</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
